O, children, now that I have completed this book, which is the last of the science of medicine, for the completion of which I have labored long, and through its explanations and declarations, it is clear to me that I complete for you here this treatise, which is a part of my surgical operations.
For the operation of surgery is established in our region and in our times as entirely private, despite the importance of the science of it and the evident traces of it; and there have been no substantial descriptions of it except in some small accounts in the works of the Ancients, which corrected many errors and hesitations, but have closed the understanding of it and lengthened its practice.
And it is evident to me that I should vivify that order in this treatise according to the way of explanation and declaration and abbreviation; and for the forms of the surgical instruments such as cautery tools and other implements of the work to be added through the declaration and preparation, which are necessary causes.
More than that, the reason why a good craftsman does not place his hand well in this our time is because the art of medicine is long and that his actor before this must be exercised in the science of anatomy, which Gualia knew, entering that he was acquainted with the youth of the members and their forms, and the conjunction and separation of them; and had knowledge of the bones, the nerves, and the tendons, and the number of them, and their integrity; and of the arteries and veins, active and quiet, and of the places of the contraction of them.
And for this, Hippocrates says that in the small work, but more so in the art of the hand.
More than that, we have already spoken of this in the introduction to this book; for who does not know what we said about anatomy will easily fall into error, which can lead to the deaths of many people, as I have seen too many such cases. For some are formed in this science but fall back into the errors of those sciences and experiences.
For you saw a doctor who fell ill and inflicted an ap斯塔西奥病于一个妇女的颈部，因误切了一些颈动脉，致使妇女流血过多而死。
And there was another doctor who almost removed a stone from a man who had been in his state for a long time, and the stone was large, and it came to him, and he extracted that stone using a piece of the bladder, so that that man died on the third day.
And I have already called for the stone to be extracted, and I see that due to the size of the stone and the position of the patient, he will likely die.
And there was another doctor who took a stipend from a duke of our land for surgery, and he came upon a black slave who had a fracture in the patient's thigh; and because of the doctor's ignorance, he extracted the fracture, over the wound, with pillows and splints of strong structure, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
And then the dislocation according to his desires, and then the reattachment, and then let it rest for a few days, and command us to release the ligament; and thus remain until the thigh and foot are well healed, and proceed to recovery.
And I was called to him, and prepared to release the ligament, and tranquility and an attempt to alleviate his pains was achieved.
But however, since corruption was confirmed in the member, I could not restrain that, and did not cease to walk the corruption in the member during the illness.
And I saw another doctor who incised a cancerous abscess, and it became ulcerated over several days, during which the evil increased greatly in him and in his lord.
The cause is that the pain is purely of melancholic humor, and does not affect everything entirely, but rather affects a member that suffers from being attacked by it.
And for this reason, my children, it is necessary for you that the operation be devised in two deviations: one where the operation is associated with health, and one where the work is perilous in the major dispositions.
And I have already existed here in all this chapter where the operation is filled with error and fear; therefore, it is necessary for you to keep this and leave that, so that the leaves do not find a way to speak against you and dishonor you.
And therefore take your weapons with diligence and protection of God, and your patients with joy and firmness.
And use the best way through the grace of God seeking salvation and praiseworthy success, and lay aside the terrible illnesses difficult to heal, and oppose your weapons to what fears you, so that sitting in your faith and in your name you do not falter: for more remains to your glory, and greater still in the world and beyond in your sanctities.
Gualia already dissected in some surgical cases: Do not treat illness wrongly, so that bad doctors are not named.
And I have already dedicated this treatise according to three chapters.
Begin the division of the treatise, and first of the first part. The first chapter ordered in the foot, regarding the forms of the instruments and the tools of the cautery, and what is necessary in the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter, on drying and perforation, and on suction cups, and on plaigs, and on extraction of arrows and similar, all chaptered and ordered by the forms of the instruments.
The third chapter, on restoration and dislocation, and on the cure of tortoises and similar; chapter ordered by the head between the feet, and by the forms of the instruments.
Know the quality of those coals for the cautery and the harms from them, and in what condition the cautery should be prohibited.
Therefore, I say that the discourse on the quality of the cautery coal and its harm is long and prolix, subtle by science, and secretly hidden; and much has already been said about it by wise men, and they are in disagreement. For my part, I content myself with a little from their sermons, to avoid excessive length.
And thus say that cautery benefits all complexions universally which is of or has matter, except two complexes, which are complexes of seminal matter.
In the complex of gout and dry matter, it becomes desiccated; for some said that cautery is beneficial for that, while others said the opposite, that cautery is not suitable in illness which is due to quality and dryness, for the nature of fire is quality and dryness, and it is inappropriate that such an illness, which is gout and dry, be healed by what is hot and dry.
And say to those who say the opposite, that by cautery one is cured in all gout and dry illness that comes in men's bodies, for when you compare the body of a man to its humors in relation to the complex of fire, you find the body hot.
And I say according to his speech, for I have already experienced this several times myself.
However, I do not claim to have experienced this as one who has been extensively trained in the Capitol of Cautery through recent exercise, and who knows the diversity of human complexions and the disposition of illnesses in their manifestations, and the causes of those, and the accidents related to them, and the span of time for those.
In other complications, there is no need for fear, and especially in wet and inflammatory diseases, since all doctors are agreed on those, and do not differ regarding the use of cautery in such cases.
Understand, children, that the secret of curing by cautery with fire and its goodness lie in the burning medical instrument, for the fire is simple, its action reaching only the member being cauterized and causing no significant harm to other members it touches.
Yet the action of the burning medical instrument reaches to those members which it touches, and strongly makes come into the affected member a disease that is difficult to cure and quickly afflicts it.
Yet fire, by its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does nothing but cause superfluous heat. We are already well aware of this through experience and long service in studying the art regarding the true causes; and for this reason, I excuse myself from the length of my discourse. If it were not that this is not written at liberty in this pause, and to reveal your secret about fire, its quality of operation on bodies, and its expulsion, which you use to expel diseases, I would deliver a philosophical demonstration, which would be useful for your people.
And know, sons, that they disagree about the time at which it is convenient to perform cautery and when is the best season of spring.
And I say that cautery is convenient at all times, because the damage due to accidental weather changes is submerged in the youth of what is affected by the cautery, and especially if the cautery is for pains or necessary pains, strong wounds, and fissures, which do not suffer delay because it is feared that those caused by malice are greater than small damage entering through time.
And thus do not trust in these, sons, for they esteem only the common people and the foolish doctors, since they say that the illness that is cured by cautery is not constant at all times, and they withhold this knowledge.
And the reason is not thus because they consider it so, for cautery is not but a method in medicine which alters the composition and dries the humors, which are the cause of venous pains.
But still, excessive cautery over medicine for the swiftness of its validity and virtue of its operation and greatness of its lord.
And it is possible that the patient's illness returns at some point in time, according to the nature of the illness, its location, and its virtue, as well as what is prepared in the body from the aggregation of superfluities in it, and what is received by it in its acquisition through food and likenesses of those causes; but if the illness where cautery is administered is a subtle illness in a member with few superfluities and humidities, like cautery for toothache due to pain and similar to that, it is possible that such pain does not return, but this is done in small quantities.
And more common speech is that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, and it is the language of surgeons, not what we understand by it, for I believe it is not a cure that helps either medicine or any other cause except cautery.
And the cause is the opposite of this; and the understanding that cautery is the last remedy of medicine is only when one administers the methods of cure for some illnesses, and those medicines do not work, and at the end of the cause, one administers cautery, which helps in that. And at this point, the last remedy of medicine is a cautery, not according to the understanding which I understand of the vulgar and too many of the foolish doctors.
And the ancients said that a cautery of gold is better than one made of iron, and they did not say this only because of the equality of gold and the sublimity of its substance.
And they said that the place for a cautery does not hurt much, since it is not absolutely severed, for I have applied it and tested it, and found that it does not do so in all bodies as in others, and a gold cautery is good and better than iron thus they say; but when you make a cautery with fire of gold, it is not up to you, for it ignites according to the quantity you want due to the reactivity of the gold, and it prepares to receive flame; and if you adjust over the ignition, the gold melts by the fire, and cases in the fire some sheets so that the artisan can cut by the occupation of that.
And for this, you should apply the iron cautery more lightly and more precisely to the correct position of the operation.
And I have already ordered this chapter concerning the cautery according to other chapters, and I have ordered those of the foot in the caput, so that I delay the request of the patient what he wants from me.
The first chapter.
This cautery addresses the cold and humidity over the servery accident of which there are two causes, these being the cause of soda and many traumatic fluxes, called corissa, from the head to the parts of the neck and the ears flowing, and many sleepiness, and tooth pain, and the gullet, and universally all illness that comes through coldness, such as paralytically, soda, and apoplexy, and similar symptoms in those illnesses.
The form of this cautery is as follows: first, you command the patient to be evacuated with a medicinal laxative for the head, for three or four nights, according to the power of the illness and the age of the patient and their habits.
And then command him to place his head on a pillow, and place that cushion between your hands on a sloping bench so that he rests his hands on his own foot.
And then place the edge of your palm near his mouth on the razor between his heels. But more importantly, since the right place has been found, mark that place with a needle, and then heat the olive cautery of which this is the form:
And then place the heated cautery over the marked spot with a needle, in such a way that it descends gradually, and your hand is gradually pressed firmly, while you rotate it.
And then lift your hand slightly and examine the spot, and if you see any part of the bone being revealed through the skin, lift your hand as much as the amount of flesh has been burned away. If not, return your hand to that iron or another, if it is cooled, so that what I have said can be seen on the bone.
And then take a little of salt and dissolve it over the area and leave it for three days.
And then place yourself over the inflamed wound and leave it there until the scar of the fire is destroyed. And then cure the area with ointment of tetrafarmacum until it is healed.
And we have said that when the wound is opened wide, it heals better, for it is better and more beneficial.
And some of them say that the joint should be cauterized inside the bone, and that the cautery should remain until a part of the bone's surface is charred.
And then scrape what is burnt from the bone, and then cure it.
And others say that the cautery should reach the marrow, pressing forcefully into the bone until it chars, and this is the method of Alphcatai. And they believe that from that place exhale the vapors of the head.
And let the wound be kept open for a long time, and soon it will be cured once it is consolidated.
But I have not seen these two kinds of cautery for all, only in some men according to the way of fear; and leave that one, I advise you, it is better for health when it is; whereas the head is developed by solution of continuity of the head as we have testified in other members, and especially when the head of the patient is of cold nature.

Chapter VI.
On the cautery for the wound.
The wound which is cured and treated with a cautery is only due to the substances that flow through phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases.
Avoid using the cautery for the substance that flows due to dryness or spasms of the nerve.
When you cure that substance of the wound with jerris, capipurgi, and guarismes, and your treatment does not bring relief, then when you treat the disease with three cauteries: the first, the hole of the ear; the second, a small opening in its vicinity; and the third, the junction of two lips.
And place your cautery on the opposite side of the malaise, for relief only comes to the part that appears healthy.
The method of cautery is to apply the cautery on the outer side of the ear near a small area above the corner of the mouth, and on the temple, where the length of the application is according to the length of the upper lip, and then place your hand over the area until the quantity of the matter of the scabby lesion is burned.

And place your hand over the area as described, keeping it treated until it is healed.

Chapter XVII.
On the cautery treatment of a fistula in the lacrimal gland of the eyelid.
When you cure a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases and do not apply your cure, then when you cauterize it according to this manner: command the patient to place his head in your lap, and let some minister hold the back of his head between your hands in such a way that it is neither hurt nor agitated.
And then place the cautery on the vein in the foot or on the wart of a blister over the heel.
And then ignite the cautery, the form of which is as follows:
which is round, as formed like a cane or a bird's claw, from one end of which the cautery is made.
And if you wish, penetrate it into the other end. And if you want, let it be drawn out like a tent.
But nonetheless, that which is concave is better for your work.
And then press the fistula if it is opened, and draw from it clean and dry that which comes out. And if it is not opened, then open it and extract the pus from it.
And then place the well-ignited cautery over it, and hold your hand a little above the nose, so that your hand does not err or the patient be disturbed, and then place the cautery on the nostrils and destroy that area.
And so, if at the beginning of your cautery it enters into the mouth, that is good; and if not, then iterate the cautery one or two times, as needed; and leave it thus for three days, and then place your hand over that spot to keep it dry until it heals.

Capitol XLVI.
Of the cautery treatment for a tornio (likely a surgical term or condition).
When pain persists in certain members due to closure or percussion and does not respond to medical treatment over a long period, then you should sear it with a pointed cautery.
And the cautery should be applied to the entire member according to its size and smallness, its virtue and depth, and the location of the tornio and pain.
So if it is healed by the first cautery, that is good; but if not, then repeat the cautery on it; for customarily, those pains are pierced in a member near the one where they occur, so that you may achieve the desired effect by the cautery while the patient is healed.
Chapter XLVII.
Of the cautery treatment for leprosy.
Lepers are sometimes treated with a large cautery for a long time, especially when the species of leprosy is caused by the putrefaction of flame and melancholy.
And so, if you want to cautery treat that area, consider whether the leprosy is common and similar to one we have cured as described in the division, neither of which it is. Be wary of the patient's condition where corruption might encompass his entire body and all its complexities; therefore, cautery the affected area on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the head, leaving space between them, and ending at the forehead by the hairline; two over the horns; and one behind, on the neck or servant (muscle).
And finish your hand with a cautery slightly inside where it leaves a small impression in the cheek, so that the expulsion of thick vapors is alleviated. Cauterize over the cheek as needed.
And if leprosy is already spread over the thigh and manifestly apparent, then you cauterize that area as well as those cauterizations which we said in the head; on the extremity of the nose, and on two cauterizations on both eyebrows, and on two cauterizations on two vertebrae of the neck, and on six cauterizations on the vertebrae of the back, and a large one near the knee, one on the kneecap, and two on the ankles, one on each ankle, and two on the heels, one on each heel, and two on the knees, and two on the muscles, and two on the tendons of his foot; cauterize that on all joints of the fingers of the hand and of the feet, and on each heel of his feet, and on the bones of his legs.
And guard the nerves which are over the heel that you do not burn those.
And sometimes cauterization is done with one cauterization on the bone of the pelvis and another on the entrance to the stomach, and another on the liver.
And know that the more tightly you adjust the cautery, the more beneficial and effective it is; and know that the patient does not feel pain in the cautery as they do elsewhere, since the patient's body is already numbed.
And know that the cautery should be large or small according to the limb and joints as indicated by the specifications of the instruments.
And then cure the cautery with a mixture of burned flour and honey, as well as other treatments until it is healed.

Chapter II.
On the cautery for corroding.
Corroding is a gradual corruption in the limb, which corrodes it as fire consumes dry wood.
Therefore, if you find the corroding in a location where you intend to apply a cautery with fire, then heat the cautery with several small and large coals as appropriate for that location where the corrosion occurs.
And then cautery that completely, as you eradicate all the corrosion and do not leave any cause of it.
And after that let it be for three days, and place a hot cloth over the cauterized areas until all the scabs have fallen off and all the corruption is gone.
And then cure that with ointment generating flesh.
But if after three days the flesh grows healthy in the area where there is no corruption, that is good; but if not, then iterate the cautery over what is raw in the corrupted areas.
And after medicating with some sharp medicines several times, use half of it in place of the cautery. But however, a cautery with fire is beneficial for superficial wounds.
And I have already described the treatment with sharp medicine in the division, so use it when you need it.

Chapter VII.
On the Treatment of Ear Abscesses.
Sometimes children inherit the cavities of their parents' non-perforated ears, and this happens in some adults as well, with an abscess in the meat of the ear due to a wound or without any apparent cause; sometimes this abscess forms in the preauricular region which does not show external signs, and sometimes it occurs in the outer parts.
And that which occurs in the region of the loins, which does not present a visible wound, is in the major dispositions of difficult recovery.
And in that where you can see the wound, make sure that you place the patient in the sun and look at it. And if you see an apparent abscess, open that with a thin lancet from which this is the form:
If the extremity of the lancet where the width is small, and one part is acute while the other is not; and the lancet has two points to prevent it from lodging in the ear.
And if the abscess is in hidden flesh in the ear or in the meat of the ear, then use thin lancets and incise that area forcefully until all the flesh is exposed.
And if the abscess is in the region of the ear, then take a thin pointed lancet and heat that iron a little in fire, and place it in the flesh of the ear.
And so, if you sense an abundance of that which the patient suffers due to difficulty in urination, increase the pressure on it by means of urination; and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear.
And then place the cloth over the ear according to the amount of swelling you have wrapped in the Egyptian ointment; and do this for several days until you are sure of the healing of the wound; or that you insert some and press it into water and powder it over the dry trissar, using it; and if you see the ear already perforated, then remove the pus and replace it with another liquid which you wrap in a cloth made of linseed oil, until the abscess is drained; and cure it as it heals.
But if a bloody flux occurs, then submerge the sponge or cloth in fresh water, wring it out, and place it over the ear, and use the other treatment which constricts the flow of blood, which is called in the treatise on distillation.
Chapter VIII.
For the care of swelling which occurs in the eyelids.
Swelling of the eyelids which sometimes become moist, at other times dry.
Then take those that have been heated or boiled, and incise them over the swelling of their eyelids, and place your hand over the areas just applied.
But if there is pain with a flow of warm blood, then cauterize those points with a thin cautery.
And the best cautery is over the incisions, and the wounds heal when there remains any cause of their swelling; and when they are cauterized with fire, those swellings are burned and do not return.
Chapter IX.
Care for great swelling in the eyelids.
Swelling in the eyelids of the eye sometimes occurs due to some cause which is similar in its strength and hardness, and for this reason it is called great swelling.
And it is an addition of thick humidity in the eyelid above and below.
And the operation in them is that you consider whether the enlargement is present in it where appears from the eyelid and is palpable at all parts; and the cause of it is slight.
And make a incision there for its width, and then probe it from all parts with ease as you evacuate, and suspend it by an ounce and cut it off.
And if the figure is large, then you adjust it with sutures; and care for it until it is healed.
And if it is small, you will not suffer harm from it because the ointment of it restores and heals it.
And if the enlargement is decreasing in the parts inside the eyelid, you adjust the inner surface, then evacuate the eyelid and suspend the enlargement by an ounce, or another you choose for incision, and press it from all parts. If the eyelid is stretched by incision, this is noted in no cause.
And at the beginning, wash the area with salted water; and dress the place with a dressing until it is healed.

Capitol.xl.
In which the main discourse on carbuncles and their sections is presented.
The carbuncles are special nodes, of various types, according to the memory of them, for each one in this treatise.
And they are diverse in their perforation and section by two methods. Of which one is according to the type of carbuncles themselves; and through this, we address the humors.
And the second method is for the places where bodily accidents occur, for a carbuncle that occurs on the head is different from one that occurs on the foot; and a carbuncle in a fleshier location is different from one at a joint; and for each of them, their judgment is made through operation.
And more of abscesses some of which cover that they not be pierced but at maturity of the health in those or complement of their.
And other abscesses some of which cover that they be lanced when crossed, and are not matured according to their complement, thus as abscesses that are near the joints, for an abscess which is near a joint, its nature is extended into what is in the circuit of it, and greatly corrupts the ligaments or nerves of that joint, making a cause of contraction of that member; or is an abscess near a principal member, and if you delay the lancing of it until it is matured it will affect the principal member; or is near the anus, therefore lance what is not mature; and do not lance crudely, for lack of digestion, but one near the anus, so that it does not cause prolapse and be extended to the internal parts of the anus, making a fistula, or done in the term where it is not healed. And you must know the time for lancing the abscess, and this is when it is matured.
And know that it is ripe when there is a decrease in pain and fever, and the reduction in swelling and pulse, and the acuteness of the head of the abscess, and other signs.
And know that when you can perceive the perforation cauterized in the location just below the abscess and from pus coming from the cure of the prominence.
And the perforation should be made along the length of the flesh or body, if the abscesses are in the thigh or feet, and at the location of the lacert, the cords of the nerves, the arteries; and, finally, in all locations where there is no reflection; for in those that are reflective, use perforation according to that member.
When the abscess is in a fleshly location, it is better to delay the perforation until the digestion of the pus is confirmed according to our saying; for if you perforate it before that, it will prolong the course of the pus and increase the hardness and depth of the lesion.
More abscesses are perforated according to the width of the flesh or body as the need dictates, or according to that from which the member suffers.
And ensure that for small abscesses, you perform a small perforation, and for large abscesses, a large and wide or multiple sections according to the diversity of the size of the abscesses.
And in other abscesses, ensure that the cord is returned to its cavity and cut, when this is done, do so quickly, as you would do in cases of tumors and buboes.
And of those that are cut with three angles in sections; and of those in which the incision is made as a figure of a mulberry leaf, as with abscesses of boils.
And of these, those in which circular and crescent-shaped sections are administered, and resemble those.
More for those in which none is done as such, where the abscesses are superficial, ensure that you perform them with a superficial perforation, or flat one only.
And when the abscess is large and has already gathered some healthy pus, that you perforate it and do not cut so as to drain all the poison at that time; having extracted a part, then raise the abscess on another day, and extract a larger part, and proceed to make punctures regularly according to degree until it is fully discharged.
And especially if the patient is a young man with virile virtue, or a woman in labor, or a small child, or an old person in decrepitude, for the animal spirit resolves into the exit of the healthy pus, and greatly weakens the disease, and you openly manage it.
Take great care with this chapter, and in your perforation where you perforate these abscesses, ensure that you cleanse the wounds and consider whether the wound of the abscess is small, or a flat section, then administer only a portion of li or coto antic; and if the abscess is large, and the fissures of the perforation are deep, then you should place your hand in each tract until they heal together.
And if in the abscess you have divided a part of the cord or have concaved it in the circuit, then you should complete it with linen cloth or thread made of li fabric, just as when you have drawn out pieces or roots, considering their moisture; strengthen it on the third day; and proceed with it and cure it according to what is appropriate from the ointments until it is healed.
And if you happen to experience bleeding during the time of your operation, then administer water mixed with wine in which you soak a cloth, and place that over the location of the blood flow for several minutes.
And if the bleeding persists, then you must administer treatment and cure with powders which I have recommended in many places of this our book and division.
And if it is in the time of winter, and the location of the abscess is near many nerves, then you must apply powders in wine and oil with a cautery, and place those over the areas.
And if it is in the summer, and the areas are fleshy, then you must place powders soaked in water and oil or in wine and oil, all of which be mixed thoroughly by the third day, as we have said, and then you must incise the abscess and cleanse that area, and administer to its cure what is suitable for it until it heals.
And this is what is necessary concerning the knowledge of the cure of abscesses generally, but according to the way of distinction, I have already said everything about the abscess regarding the method of its cure specifically.

Of the section on abscesses in the vein of the head.
In the vein of the head, small abscesses, and their species of knots which contain tunics that are made thus; and the species of these are spots.

Chapter LXV.
Of the cure for intestinal hernia.
The occurrence of this hernia is due to a separation that extends over the diaphragm covering the abdomen from the pelvic bones. Because of this rupture in the membrane, some of the intestines protrude.
And this rupture is either of the diaphragm or of its excision. This happens to these two species due to various causes: perhaps a blow, or by jumping, or by shouting, or by lifting some heavy cause, or by a similar action.
And the sign of this, when it is due to extension of the diaphragm, is that it occurs gradually over a long period of time and does not happen suddenly. It is an abscess that enters the chest through the membrane because the diaphragm contains the intestine.
And the sign of this is when it is due to separation of the diaphragm, for at the beginning it causes sudden and intense pain; it is an abscess that appears different from the surrounding area. This is due to the protrusion of the intestine, and the body's reaction in the parts outside the diaphragm.
And sometimes the intestine or the tissue is pushed out through the fabric, and this hernia is called intestinal carbuncle.
And sometimes it is caused by distension, and sometimes a hole forms in the intestine, where it gets stuck, and this causes great discomfort to the patient, and sometimes it leads to severe pain, especially when pressed.
And in the treatment of the symptoms of this illness there is fear, because it is suspected that the cure should avoid the spread to that area.
And the method of the operation is that you command the patient to push the intestine back into its cavity with their hand at the internal parts of their cavity if it obeys on its return, and then fix them over their shoulder between your hands, and lift their legs.

And seek around the thumbs that they know that there is no cause for the intestine enveloped in the white cord. But if you find any cause for it, then peel that away and leave it on the abdomen.
And then incise in the part below the scrotum along a section from which fluid and pus flow as we have recounted in what we have said.
And then apply wool submerged in oil, and place it on the wound; apply the lint we have mentioned (and several times the white chalk is seared, which we have already said near the incision of their fear of a flow of blood, because often this happens) and leave the lint inside so that it may fall by itself.
And if the application is delayed, then pour cold water on it, and place it there until it falls as we have said.
And then heal the wound with another treatment for wounds as it heals.
Capitol. lxvi.
Of hernia ventosa.
In this hernia, nothing has been seen that was burned during the treatment of it.

Chapter LXVII.
Of the disorder that occurs in the ankles.
Sometimes there is a rupture in the ankles as we have said, and apply ointment to the area.
And the surgeons do not attribute any cause of the ruptures to the intestines; and if they do, it is rare; and return them in all hours.
But if the time is prolonged, there is an appropriate crack in the cavity where we place the intestine; and this accident occurs due to the extension of the cavity, which is in the ankles as we have said, the cause being that the cavity is stretched, and then softened, and the area becomes suppurated, and apply ointment.
And the treatment of it is with a cautery as described in the preceding account.
And sometimes it is cured by applying iron according to this manner: and that the patient lies on his side between your legs, and then the place of the rupture of the pustules dries up and exudes fluid according to the width as per the quantity of three fingers.
And then strengthen the white ointment that is at the wound once it is uncovered.

Chapter LXXXVIII.
On the mollification of the scrotal skin.
When spots appear on the scrotal skin in some men, the skin is mollified because the flesh between there is also mollified, and attention should be paid to this.
Then it is necessary for the one who is in charge of the treatment to ensure that the patient lies in such a way as to facilitate the healing, and completely expose the scrotal area that is mollified over the natural scrotum; and then carefully bring the two lips together at the suture.
And if you wish, make three or four initial stitches in the excess of the mollified scrotal area and then perform a firm suture.
And then cut between the stitches; and after curing other wounds, allow the threads to dissolve.
Capitol lxix.
Of castration.
Know that castration in our law is excommunicated, but by cause it is told to me that I should remember it in this book; and the recall of this is not necessary for two reasons, one of which is that when a doctor is questioned about it, he knows the cure for whom it happens. The other reason is that we must sometimes have castration of other beasts for our cattle, such as bulls, boars, and pigs, and similar to beasts.
And thus say that castration is done in two ways: either by atrisssion or by a sectional incision.
But in that which is done by atrisssion, the way of the operation is that we cut the beast in water so that the genitals of the beast are softened and relaxed while they hang. And then take those with your hand so that they are relaxed and no marks appear upon touch.
In castration performed due to fissure and secution, ensure that you have the beast and press the cord of the testicles with your left hand.
Then lift the suspensory, and incise over each groove between two testicles.
Then incise those pus that you have from each excoriation. And do not leave on those of the scrotum any cause, but the fine incision which is over the veins.
And this method of castration is better which is performed by traction, for traction strongly leaves no cause of the testicles because the beast desires copulation.
Then cure the wound while it is healing.
Capitulum LX.
On the cure of hermaphroditism.
Hermaphroditism in males occurs according to two methods: one where a gap appears in the cord of the testicles, in which there is a figure resembling a female between the two testicles.
And sometimes a flow of urine comes from that cord in the scrotum.
In women, it is special: and the woman's mons pubis is like two testicles of a man slightly swollen on the outer part like the scrotum of a man with its two testicles.
And the treatment is of three kinds: two for men and one for women. And you should incise those tight muscles where the fluid escapes from that area, and then treat those with the cure for other wounds.
And in the second kind for men from which urine comes from the cord of the testicles, neither treatment nor operation is needed.

Lymph nodes that are firm and tight are due to natural causes where they are compressed and appear noticeable; sometimes in women, they are enlarged to such an extent that they expand like in men, and can be felt during intercourse.
Then hold the superfluous phlegm in your hand or cupped hand and insert it.
And do not insert it too deeply, especially in the region of the rectum, so that no flux of sand occurs.
And then attend to that for the cure of the wounds until they are healed.
More hidden flesh is flesh that does not appear in the horror of the womb until it fills that space; and a large cyst is situated near the parts external according to the likeness of a cocoon (and for this some first called it "caudate illness"); therefore, handle it as we would cut phlegm, and cure it until it is healed.
Capitol.lix.
On the cure of hernia.
Hernia is when the wall of the woman's womb is perforated, or is torn slightly. And it can be natural or accidental.
An accident occurs due to a malfunctioning condition that has preceded, and that is caused by meat not fitting well or by a subtle or thick chip.
It is caused in the region of the uterus, or in its sides, or in the upper part of it, or in the lower part of it, and you prohibit coitus and impregnation and childbirth, and strongly you prohibit menstruation.
The knowledge of that is made through the examination of the midwife, if the obstruction is obvious, promptly; but if it is not obvious, then you seek that area with your fingers or with a probe.
But if the obstruction is due to a subtle chip, and is near the two lips, then you probe and dislodge that.
And you place powders on the two lips, and then place your fingers indicating both hands in front of them.
And the woman is on her back, her thighs extended, and then spread the two lips with force while that subtle chip is broken and the obstruction is opened.
And then take wool and soak it in oil, place it over the area, and keep someone there to prevent the incised area from becoming consolidated.
If the ulcer is large and deep, then you must incise it with a spatula or a leaf of mint.
If the ulcer is superficial, then suspend it with a wick, and incise it.
And use those medicines that stop the flow of venom from a bite, such as vervain, dragon's blood, and garlic, prepared with honey.
And then administer a wide lead cannula to prevent the wound from becoming only slightly consolidated.
And keep it for a few days and administer weak wine.
And then use the other consolidation remedy while it is healing.
And sometimes accidents occur in the predominant state of other tissues, then you must incise according to this manner. If this is due to a chronic abscess, in the chronic abscess which is in the major part do not make any counter-irritation in any manner.
Capitol LXXIII.

Chapter 74.
On the perforation of the vein in the thigh.
Various specific forms of apothem (a type of abscess) occur in the thigh, such as carbuncle, apothema lapident, ulcer, adhubelat, erpetromens, fistulas emoryas, raguarrias, thyly, and other apothemas. Then consider whether the pain in the abscess at its beginning is acute upon percussion and flux and fever, and sometimes that it turns red and if it feels like a perforation inside, and treat it with what helps towards maturity until the acuity of the accidents ceases.
Then you should place the woman on a bench that has two benches; recline her on her side and adjust her feet to the part behind her abdomen, and spread her thighs apart, and place her arms beneath her armpits, with her hands resting on her sides.
Then the midwife should follow the vein straight and administer the instrument through the openings of the uterus, the form of which will come in the cases that will be discussed soon.
When you want to administer this instrument, place it along the length of the uterus, and what part of the instrument enters the uterus should not exceed the length of the uterus and expel the disease. But if the instrument is larger than the size of the sore, then cover it with powder over the sore's size so that no part of the instrument enters the sore.
And cover it so that the fluid that flows in the needle passes above and that the minister holds the needle and rotates the fluid within until the openings of the sore are open.

And sometimes the liver and wound are washed and tried with chrismated water and honey, then with water in which is stirred rye or barley flour, and then returned to ointment.
And if the wound is inside the liver softened, then covet that you be prohibited from treating it with iron, but take care that you do as we have said in the division.
Capitol.lix.

Chapter LXXVI.
On the extraction of the fetus when it is dead.
When you treat the dead fetus as we have said in the division of medicine and it is not outside the body, then you must use surgery if necessary. You should consider whether the woman is in good health and not affected by any of the conditions for which her life is feared to be in danger.
When the woman is laid on her back with her head inclined sideways and her thighs elevated.
The minister should hold that [part] with two hands or tied on the bed so that the body does not extend during the extraction.
Then apply to the mouth of the patient some sweet-smelling oil and oil of almond and fenugreek and sesame.
Then the midwife should anoint her hand with those oils and ointments, and place her hand with ease in the patient's mouth, and seek with her hand the location where the fingers should be placed on the fetus.
Place the fingers accordingly: then consider if the fetus is ready to be born by placing your fingers at its temples, or on its neck, or in its mouth, or palate, or leave the beard area, or on the furrow of the chest, or on the proper locations of the ribs, or leave the hypochondria.
And if the discharge is from his feet, at the ankle, or in the middle of the back.
And hold the thumb with your right hand, curve it at that location which is between the fingers of your left hand, insert your hand easily and place the thumb in one of those locations which we have mentioned, until you reach the root cause.
And place and hold the other thumb, or the third if necessary, so that it is in equal opposition, and not extension according to its straightness solely.
And gently move it in all directions, so that the tension of the tooth is relieved as is done in dental extraction.
And hold it in such a way that the extension is softened; and if any part of it is retained, then have the midwife apply some of her fingers with oil and insert them expertly and rotate around the part that is retained.
So if the part of the flesh is forgotten, then the nails may grow into that place; and do this while all the flesh is retracted.
But if the hand is placed in front of the other, and it is not possible to reduce it due to the constriction, then cover that part with a cloth; and then extract it while all of it is retracted, and incise it either at the joint of the hand or in its side.
And do the same with the other hand and both feet.
But if the head of the flesh is large, or you encounter constriction during incision, or it is in the head with accumulated water, then you must insert sponge-tipped forceps between the fingers and cut open the head to drain the water, or use a scoop-like instrument called "alundat," the shape of which will be shown in the forms of other instruments in the chapter that follows this.
And do the same if the flesh has a large head by nature: then you must incise it with a hooked knife, or use an alundat as we have said; and then extract the bones with forceps.
And if the head is swollen and constricted, you should lift the sternum, then cut where the humidity which is in the feet has infiltrated.
And if it is not complicated, nor obstructed by swelling, then you should incise the head as soon as possible according to what is convenient for you.
And if the swelling of the abdomen is suppurated or in edema, then you should perforate it where the humidity that is in it flows.
And if the abscess is on their feet, then the draw of it is light and its direction to the mouth of the vein is light.
And if it is constricted, you should incise the abdomen and feet, then you should extract that with a cloth which you have wrapped around your hand, and incise the abdomen and feet where what is within flows out.
And if the other members are swollen and return to normal, then the surgeon should insert her left hand; and if the mouth of the vein is opened, then she should insert her hand in the prehensor of layre, and seek for the head, and pull that with the fingers into the mouth of the vein, and quickly insert one or two uncia, and pull them with those.
And if the mouth of the main vein is narrowed by an abscess, when it happens to someone, then ensure it is not twisted; first, ensure that you administer effusion of fatty humid causes. And administer poultices; and follow the patient with waters that soften and moisten.
And if the wound is on the side, then if possible, punctuate it: and administer what we have said about the living wound.
And if that is not possible, then incise it in pieces, and extract it.
And ensure that you do not leave any cause inside the wound.
And when you have completed your operation, then administer what we have said about the treatment of abscesses caused by an abscess in the main vein.
And if there is a flow of blood, then apply compresses with astringent waters and administer the other treatment.
And I have already seen a woman in her womb where one child was dead, and nearby another pregnancy began, and the dead child is no longer present. It happens that after a long time an abscess in the inguinal region; and when opened, it is filled with pus, and begins to discharge blood.
And I was called to treat it, and treated it for a long time, and the wound did not heal completely.
Then I applied plaster with strong adhesive properties over it, and set one splint, and after some days, set another splint; and I was greatly amazed, for in the thigh there is no bone.
And then I realized that they were the bones of the dead child.
Then I dressed the wound, and extracted bones from it, the child existing in her uterine conditions, and having witnessed such a manner for a long time, I corrected part of the arm.
And I do not consider it strange, but rather that in this there is science and aid to what the physician uses his hand for in treatment.

Form of vertigo at which the liver is opened:

For the extraction of the second child.

For the treatment of an unperforated child's anus.
When the child cries and its anus is not perforated, which have already been treated with a fine and rolled bandage. Then have the midwife perforate with her own said bandage; and if not, perforate it with a sharp instrument, and take care that it does not touch the membrane.
Then place it over the area infused with wine and oil; and cure that with ointment until it heals.

For the treatment of fistulas that occasion openings.
The fistulas that occasion openings proceed from a decay and coarseness of those parts, which occur near the buttocks or in the space of one side.
And it is either a fistula or a ulcer.
And when that decay is old and comes from watery white moisture or subtle corruption, sometimes these fistulas penetrate.
And those that penetrate are known by what occurs from them through the outflow and through windiness; sometimes the patient suffers from the outflow, and strongly is affected by those worms.
And of these fistulas, sometimes in the space they penetrate into the bladder, and into the meat of the vagina; and of those that penetrate into the joint of the thigh and into the base of the foot.
And to know whether a fistula penetrates into the buttocks or does not penetrate, you should insert your finger into the buttock and gently probe with a thin reed or iron in the fistula when there is no pus.
But if there is a tumor, then insert into that fine cavity either lead or horse skin, which you feel in your hand.
And if you do not feel that at all and proceed from no cause of passage or worm or tumor, as we have said, then know that it is non-penetrant, and then apply a cure.
And when the fistula is penetrant into the bladder or into the flesh of the groin, then its significance is dysuria from that side and prohibition thereof until the area has been medically consolidated.
But if it is penetrant into the junction of the thigh or into the bone and causes pain in the circumference, then its sign is that the tumor pervades here if there is no tumor in the bone, and pain in the circumference of the affected area; and that from it there is constant swelling; and that it does not respond to that medical treatment, nor is it consolidated by ointment.
And in all those penetrant fistulas, there is not a complete cure, and the cure of these is hard work and the diligence of the medical leaves upon which they rely.
In those that are not penetrating and not ancient, heal with iron as I will recount to you later, and what is already healed and protracted.
And it is that the patient lies on his side with his knees bent, the thighs inclined toward the abdomen, and a lead or iron catheter inserted into the fistula if it is tortuous, so that you can feel where the catheter passes.
And if the patient feels pain around the throat, then you should insert the thumb on this side into the throat.
And if you feel the catheter already by itself clearly penetrating in your thumb, or something between your thumb and the sore or flesh, then you can be certain that it is penetrating; and then do not work on that, for healing is not there, as we have said.

Of the treatment of wounds.
And I have already said in the division of the treatment of wounds what pertains to the free and with medicines according to the need.
Therefore, it is said that wounds are diverse according to where they are caused and according to the area on which they fall.
And the causes why wounds are made are thus: by a stone impact, or a sword cut or a dagger, or a lance strike, or a rod, or an arrow, or similar to those caused by such impacts.
More specifically, the wounds in the parts of the body are thus: like a wound that falls on the head, or the neck, or the foot, or the abdomen, or the thigh, or similar to those of the limbs.
And I am recommending the treatment of some wounds because you apply that reasoning and rule to other wounds.
And I will start with simple head ailments, for the recall of compound cases will come at the beginning of the third book.
So say that when an injury occurs in the head with a simple wound and it is not a fracture, consider: if it is due to a stone or similar object, and has already shattered the skull slightly only and is a large wound and you fear an evil development into an abscess, then you should probe and bleed the cephalic vein immediately, without delay; and extract from there as much blood as the power of the wound allows, provided no other reason prevents bleeding, especially if the blood that issues from the wound is little.
And the bleeding is from the opposite side of the injured wound; and one must guard against filling, and eating, and heavy foods.
But if some cause forbids reduction, then lessen the food but do not approach meat or drink.
And place your hand over the wound, if an abscess develops, apply heat with olive oil or with wine in which astringents are dissolved.
But if it is certain that an abscess has formed, then place yourself over the wound, if it is fresh with its own blood and the air has not changed that place, apply the powder which I will describe shortly.
But if the air has already changed that place, then place yourself over some ointments until it is healed.
But if the wound is large or due to a cut and the edges do not close properly with stitches, then adjust those with sutures according to the method of suturing that I will describe.
But if the wound is exposed to bone and skin, and it is not retention but only a small suspensory ligament, then incise that area and cure the wound with medicines, restore the flesh nearby in its proper place, and command the patient to eat foods in which they are accustomed: bread and those that resemble them, until it is healed.
And if you find putrefaction in the flesh and it does not adhere to the bone, then incise all of that area and let it drain, and cure it accordingly.
If in these swellings the artery or vein through which flows blood cannot be avoided, and it is not cut by medicines, then you inquire about the artery, and if you find that uncut one, you incise it with a knife or ligate it; and if necessity prompts you that what we have said does not apply, then you cauterize where the blood will be cut off.
If these swellings are simple and small, the cause of them is light; sprinkle this powder over them, for before the air changes, it will solidify there.
The manner of the powder is this: take one part olive oil of turpentine, two parts blood from a dragon, and three parts cauterized fat; mix them all well and sift them, fill the swelling with it, confine it properly within a good seal, and let it coagulate with the blood.
Then strengthen it above with powder and leave it, and do not disturb it while it is not absorbed, for the medicine will not take effect until it is healed.
And sometimes they do this solely with cautery, when in your presence there is none of dragon's blood.

Of the treatment of abscesses and fistulas.
Know that any plague or apostema when it encloses and becomes ancient, and forms a ulcer, and is not consolidated and grows a branch constantly and is not incised, then in whatever member it is, universally it is named fistula and we call it an abscess.
And according to truth, fistula is a fleshy node, hard, white at which there is no pain and at which the cavity is such as it is by the bird's wound; and for this reason, it is called that ulcer root, that is, pain.
And in that ulcer there is moisture, which grows a branch; and the strong moisture is incised within a few hours. And sometimes this moisture is thick, small, and fine.
All those causes have been shown, and the signs of them and the cure for them by medicine in this division.
And thus I will show you how to know the cure for a fistula which is caused by surgical operation with the hand.
And know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; some of these fistulas lead to the large veins and arteries, or to the nerves, or to the liver, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to one of the vertebrae, or to some joint composed thus like those of the hand and foot; and these are those that are near the main part and similar.
And thus of these fistulas that proceed in this manner they are among the maladies of difficult cure, and do not receive a cure or occupation; for such is work and ignorance.

And of the signs of poisoning are when the arrow lodges in it, passes through the bone, and is situated above the brain, which is on top of the skull, for it happens due to the strong poison, scotoma, vertigo, redness in the pupils, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile. The patient feels a heavy head, with the speech cut off and the voice destroyed, and is situated at the site of the wound white moisture resembling powder, and from it appearing like an excess of fleshiness.
And therefore if you see these signs, then abstain from the cure and extraction of the arrow, unless it is outside.
And the signs of the arrow when it is in the heart are that it is near the left nipple, and you feel a hard lump there which is not visible; and strong movement of the arrow seems like the pulse, and the flow of the dark bloody wound, and the coldness at the extremities, pallor of the face, and syncope; and therefore you would know that death descends totally hopeless.
And the signs when the arrow has wounded the lung are spitting of bloody foam from the wound, and the vessels near the throat are engorged, and the color of the patient is changed, and he exhales a great spirit or sighs for air with difficulty.
And if the arrow is in the periosteum which is in the foot, and the pain then is near the small bones, and causes a great and violent pain with much sighing, and not all the members' muscles are affected.

The species of fractures are motas, and their figures are diverse, and the causes are distinct. For some fractures, they are caused by the impact of a blow, which breaks the bone completely through the cartilage, leaving the bone like this in the wood, and for this reason, this species is named ascial; or the blow cuts part of the bone, and cuts into the flesh but does not pass beyond the surface of it; and this species of fracture is named levatio absoluta.
And the swelling of these two kinds of fractures is either great or small, and the friction fracture; its cause is a blow with a stick or a fall on a stone, and they resemble this.
And this fracture is penetrating, which nearly reaches the periosteum where the bone is located; or it is in the surface of the bone, and the swelling of these two kinds of fractures is either great or small.
And for this fracture, the bone is weakened in its fine hairiness, and for this reason, this species of fracture is named capillary.
And it is a fracture that is caused either by compression or by the strike of a stone, which causes some layer of the bone to enter the internal parts, and it occurs in the concave place as happens with the metal pans when struck and is part of their entry into the internal parts.
And most often this occurs in the bodies of wet bones, such as those of infants.
And to all these species of closed fractures, they are painful as if by separate stabs. And I will return to the recollection of all this at its location.

Third chapter.
On the restoration of the nose when it is broken.
Know that it is not broken from the nose but two parts together more overable, or one of those few times, because in it you have two bones, for the part left is cartilaginous, and is not broken, and you do not damage it but friction and tortuosity and sinuosity.

And do this for you to facilitate the operation, and guard that it does not become inflamed as a result of your procedure on the patient in pain.

And insert into the extremity of the nose a wad of linen cloth, if the fracture is in one part, or two wicks, if the fracture is in two parts, and let them fill the nostril.
And some of the ancient restorers say that the wicks should be soaked in honey, and replaced throughout the day, but this is not seen by me; instead, let the wad be soaked in honey wax powdered with flour; and leave the wick until the bone is set and the cartilage has hardened.
And sometimes insert into the nose instead of a wick, a hot cloth wrapped in linen cloth; and this is when the nasal fracture is very severe and the patient is not prohibited from breathing.
And this cause is not necessary for you; and if you wish, do this, and if you wish, use wicks.

And if the bones of the nose are broken with a small fracture or are comminuted, when you need to split those, extract them with instruments suitable for those; then close the incision, treat that with what encases and consolidates, and use plasters as appropriate.
And if a plague occurs inside the nose, when you need to treat that with washes and administer lead pipes until it is completely healed.
Chapter IV.
On the restoration of the jaw when broken.
When the jaw is broken and the fracture is not open, consider whether the fracture is only superficial, and not broken into two pieces but bent inward, in which case the perception is light.
And thus, if the fracture is on the right side, you should introduce the left index finger into the mouth of the patient; similarly, if the fracture is on the left jaw, then introduce the right index finger; and push the swelling of the fracture inward with ease to the parts outward, with your other hand from the part outward of the bone; do this properly so that it goes well.
And if the fracture of the jaw is already separated into two parts, then you should apply extension to both parts according to straightness so that the alignment of the bone is possible.

Chapter VIII.
For the restoration of the ribs when they are fractured.
Know that fractures of the ribs do not occur except in large spaces between them; and at their ends at the front part, such contact does not cause fracture since they are cartilaginous. And the knowledge of this is not hidden from the feeling; you must inquire about it with your fingers.

For this reason, you place a cloth over the bone; and it results in difficulty in breathing, coughing, and vomiting due to spasm; and this is of difficult cure.
And already the Ancients were ingenious in such matters.
And they say that by placing food in the patient's mouth that causes inflammation and swelling, the belly will become swollen and extended, and the fracture will be pushed outward.
But let us consider this so that it is not a trivial cause for generating a carbuncle; and if it does happen, then aid the patient.
And some of them say that it should be placed above the windpipe and near where pus will form with strength; this seems like a reasonable argument, but nevertheless, it is feared that the windpipe might carry the superfluities to that place due to weakness.
And some of them say: cover the area with wool that has been submerged in oil, and let it be packed with powder between the ribs until it is full, ensuring the dressing fits snugly as you wrap it according to the shape; and treat the patient with therapy involving food and medicine.
And if the patient is violently constrained causing pain which they cannot endure, and you make a puncture in the skin with the blade to relieve it, fear for the patient, then cut over the place, uncovering from the broken rib, and place your hand over that instrument which retains the flaps, the memory of which precedes, and incise the bone with facility, and extract it.

Chapter IX.
On the restoration of fractures of the spine in the back and neck.
In some cases, when fractures occur in the bones of the neck, and then apply friction and similar treatments to the vertebrae of the back. And if you feel along the spine of the neck and want to know if they will be cured or not, then consider the pulse in their feet.

Chapter XIII.
On the restoration of fractures of the hand and fingers.

Capitol.xxiii.
Of speech on dislocation.
Dislocation is the displacement of one of the joints of that particular place, making it forbidden to move, and distorts the shape of the limb, causing great pain and injuries in the patient.

And for this reason, it should neither be cut nor stretched during the time of gangrene, for moist wounds cause spasms and severe pains.
